<div id="review_3180441907" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3180441907" />
    <a title="Stephen Kiernan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7582177-stephen-kiernan"><img alt="Stephen Kiernan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442518399p2/7582177.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3180441907?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen Kiernan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen Kiernan" href="/user/show/7582177-stephen-kiernan">Stephen Kiernan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781933392813" href="/book/show/813624.The_Man_Who_Planted_Trees">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3180441907" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10502625293786058318">In rural Vermont where I live, the soils are predominantly clay. As a result, every home sits on a lot of five acres or more, so the septic systems cannot taint the water wells. Like nearly all of my neighbors, I actually live on a fraction of the land -- about one-third of an acre. The rest is idle (except for the enterprises of critters and birds and fireflies who are quite busy nine months of the year). <br/>I've begun a very small effort to populate the land with trees, having learned from variou</span>
  <span id="freeText10502625293786058318" style="display:none">In rural Vermont where I live, the soils are predominantly clay. As a result, every home sits on a lot of five acres or more, so the septic systems cannot taint the water wells. Like nearly all of my neighbors, I actually live on a fraction of the land -- about one-third of an acre. The rest is idle (except for the enterprises of critters and birds and fireflies who are quite busy nine months of the year). <br />I've begun a very small effort to populate the land with trees, having learned from various readings that my acreage could support perhaps 1,200 of them, and thereby offset the atmospheric carbon that I produce. If it works, I'll share surplus saplings with neighbors, and perhaps other towns, and in some years this area might serve as a kind of carbon sink -- a modest contribution to reducing the form of air pollution that currently endangers our planet. As side effects, we might see more birds and critters hereabouts too. <br />I'm no forester, and know that this idea may prove to be a pipedream. But when I discussed it with a friend, she loaned me this excellent book, which tells the story of a man in a remote region of France who turned a wasteland into a wilderness. His method? The continuous planting of trees. Saplings, really.<br />It was a great pleasure to encounter this story again, its simplicity and grace, its mythic power. This particular edition has the appeal of evocative wood carvings. It also contains some of the book's backstory, including an investigation about whether it might be true. To me, that could not matter less, because after only a few pages the reader recognizes the ring of emotional truth, which is legendary and lasting regardless of available historical facts. <br />If you haven't read this story in a few years, please treat yourself. It is a sweet reminder of the immense power of small incremental deeds. Also it is stirring, because it contains the lesson that planting a tree is a visible form of hope. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10502625293786058318" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16309941313547324896">Finished it in one sitting. And this is where Jean Giono has succeeded in his book.<br/><br/>The book is written in a very simple but realistic manner, while sending an optimistic and inspiring message. It is written so well that, for a moment, I believed the story to be actually true. Though it isn't, the book doesn't fail to imply that </span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4672812-zuberino?shelf=translation">translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4672812-zuberino?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4672812-zuberino?shelf=village-life">village-life</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4672812-zuberino?shelf=french-literature">french-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4672812-zuberino?shelf=alps">alps</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4672812-zuberino?shelf=fable">fable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4672812-zuberino?shelf=environment">environment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4672812-zuberino?shelf=provence">provence</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4672812-zuberino?shelf=rural-life">rural-life</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2406185052" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11365959103219624535">Beautiful allegory, narrated in such compelling fashion by the author as to be utterly believable - even after you find out that Giono made up the whole thing, even THEN you want to believe in the saintly goodness of the Alpine shepherd Elzeard Bouffier. Were it better known, this fable could well be a foundation text of modern day environmental movements - a bit like Carson’s Silent Spring, only different.<br/><br/>Gorgeous woodcut illustrations by Harry Brockway, that only add to the power of the text.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

In a complete solitude, without a tiniest desire of someone's admiration. <br/>Truly one of my all time favourite stories. <br/><br/>"I was left literally speechless, and as he didn't speak either we spent the whole day walking silently trough the forest. ...   <span id="freeText14829286501858568683" style="display:none">Such a beautiful tale of a man who is determined to grow a forest in an abandoned place. Despite his unfortunate circumstances and two World Wars in the background that keep on destroying — he keeps on building. In a complete solitude, without a tiniest desire of someone's admiration. <br />Truly one of my all time favourite stories. <br /><br />"I was left literally speechless, and as he didn't speak either we spent the whole day walking silently trough the forest. ... When you remembered that it had all emerged from the hands and spirit of this one man, without any technical aids, you saw that men could be as efficient as God in other things beside destruction."</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('13xFvMIMLVlTCPHkhcaa9foSI/43MogqVciwRp2JYNDtWixueVLkMfQjRYVyM5AqLE3ENvm/Bk0Otvb3UMqSSg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('B/ZVqbkHACFFBppjCFKLysO0EtoIj+9IvJZ3RY/zUt090Dx7AlnJSeItLgL/p4EVFev1EsYCYS/n6DH0QrCgRw==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/54103.Jean_Giono">About Jean Giono</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1597537817538769951">Jean Giono, the only son of a cobbler and a laundress, was one of France’s greatest writers. His prodigious literary output included stories, essays, poetry, plays, film scripts, translations and over thirty novels, many of which have been translated into English. <br/><br/>Giono was a pacifist, and was twice imprisoned in France at the outset and conclusion of World War II. <br/><br/>He remained tied to Provence and</span>
  <span id="freeText1597537817538769951" style="display:none">Jean Giono, the only son of a cobbler and a laundress, was one of France’s greatest writers. His prodigious literary output included stories, essays, poetry, plays, film scripts, translations and over thirty novels, many of which have been translated into English. <br /><br />Giono was a pacifist, and was twice imprisoned in France at the outset and conclusion of World War II. <br /><br />He remained tied to Provence and Manosque, the little city where he was born in 1895 and, in 1970, died.<br /><br />Giono was awarded the Prix Bretano, the Prix de Monaco (for the most outstanding<br />collected work by a French writer), the Légion d’Honneur, and he was<br />a member of the Académie Goncourt.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1597537817538769951" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

            <span class="readable">&ldquo;For a human character to reveal truly exceptional qualities, one must have the good fortune to be able to observe its performance over many years. If this performance is devoid of all egoism, if its guiding motive is unparalleled generosity, if it is absolutely certain that there is no thought of recompense and that, in addition, it has left its visible mark upon the earth, then there can be no mistake.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/9093076-for-a-human-character-to-reveal-truly-exceptional-qualities-one">4 likes</a>

          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Creation seemed to come about in a sort of chain reaction. He did not worry about it; he was determinedly pursuing his task in all its simplicity; but as we went back towards the village I saw water flowing in Brooks that had been dry since the memory of man. This was the most impressive result of chain reaction that I had seen. These dry streams had once, long ago, run with water.&rdquo;</span>
